<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2132c2b2-1de6-4371-a2eb-2b3af9f45e46'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_164922892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164922892" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/164922892?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer164922892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16951463065848539891"><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&current=allstarsuperman-1-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349214i/703284.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Okay</b>, other than <i>Frank Quitely</i> giving <b>Supes</b> the <b>physique</b> of a <b>championship bowler</b>, this book wasn’t bad. It certainly was <b>NOT</b> the loathsome, <b>Batman persona-raping</b> shit bomb that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2239435.All_Star_Batman_and_Robin_the_Boy_Wonder__Vol__1' title='All-Star Batman and Robin the Boy Wonder, Vol. 1 by Frank Miller' rel='nofollow noopener'>All-Star Batman & Robin the Boy Wonder, Volume 1</a> was <i>(I still haven’t forgiven you for that Frank Miller)</i>. I think that <i>Grant Morrison</i> did a good job capturing the essential, archetypal “goodness” of Superman in this homage/tribute/restoration of the icon of icons. <br/><br/>Still, this was a swing and a miss for me...though a</span>
  <span id="freeText16951463065848539891" style="display:none"><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=allstarsuperman-1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349214i/703284.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Okay</b>, other than <i>Frank Quitely</i> giving <b>Supes</b> the <b>physique</b> of a <b>championship bowler</b>, this book wasn’t bad. It certainly was <b>NOT</b> the loathsome, <b>Batman persona-raping</b> shit bomb that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2239435.All_Star_Batman_and_Robin_the_Boy_Wonder__Vol__1" title="All-Star Batman and Robin the Boy Wonder, Vol. 1 by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">All-Star Batman &amp; Robin the Boy Wonder, Volume 1</a> was <i>(I still haven’t forgiven you for that Frank Miller)</i>. I think that <i>Grant Morrison</i> did a good job capturing the essential, archetypal “goodness” of Superman in this homage/tribute/restoration of the icon of icons. <br><br>Still, this was a swing and a miss for me...though a well-intended and decently executed one (<i>i’m still looking at you Frank Miller</i>). Part of my displeasure with this is that I’m just not a huge Superman fan and I never really have been. For me, his adventures and story-lines have always lacked the reader engagement and dramatic tension that more “vulnerable” heroes are able to inspire. Therefore, take this review with a grain of kryptonite since I have never been one that drank deep from the kool-aid when it comes to the last son of Krypton.<br><br>I like my heroes more “punishing” and with a bit more “bub” in them. <br><br>That said, one of my problems with this was the timing in which I read it. I'm currently half way through Grant Morrison’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10081832.Supergods_What_Masked_Vigilantes__Miraculous_Mutants__and_a_Sun_God_from_Smallville_Can_Teach_Us_about_Being_Human" title="Supergods What Masked Vigilantes, Miraculous Mutants, and a Sun God from Smallville Can Teach Us about Being Human by Grant Morrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Supergods: What Masked Vigilantes, Miraculous Mutants, and a Sun God from Smallville Can Teach Us about Being Human</a>, a full-length non-fiction book on the history of the comic book superhero and I....LOVE...the way this guy writes. Hip, slick, punky, phrase-turning poetry that reminded me of some of his fellow SF-writing Scotsman, Iain Banks and Richard Morgan, both of whose work I love. This guy should definitely be writing novels and I hope he does so in the near future because I was blown away by his witty, grungy prose. <br><br>The problem, Houston, is that such style is non-existent here. And, as I look back, that style is non-existent in all of Grant Morrison's comic work that I've read to date. This baffles and sorta ticks me off. For someone so instrumental in increasing the visibility of the comic book form, I don’t know why he wouldn’t unleash a whole can of his breezy, attitude-laden addictive whoop ass to this medium that just screams out for it. Don’t get me wrong, the writing is fine, but reading this and then immediately switching to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10081832.Supergods_What_Masked_Vigilantes__Miraculous_Mutants__and_a_Sun_God_from_Smallville_Can_Teach_Us_about_Being_Human" title="Supergods What Masked Vigilantes, Miraculous Mutants, and a Sun God from Smallville Can Teach Us about Being Human by Grant Morrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Supergods: What Masked Vigilantes, Miraculous Mutants, and a Sun God from Smallville Can Teach Us about Being Human</a> is like alternating between Dan Brown to Dickens...jarring to say the least. <br><br><b>Readers’ Cardinal Rule #1 to writers</b>: don’t “dumb down” the prose...ever. Whether it’s YA fiction, children’s stories or comic books. Write the story and trust your audience. Now, if I wasn't currently reading Morrison’s novel and seeing first hand what a gift the man has, than I may not have been as put off by the writing.<br><br> But I am...and I was <br><br>Apart from the jarring effects of the writing disparity and the doughy pillsbury nature of the Superman rendering...<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/superheroes%20and%20villains/?action=view&amp;current=Clark_Kent_All-Star_Superman_002-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349214i/703285.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>my other problems/irritants (without giving away major spoilers) include:<br><br>1. The Atlas &amp; Samson “who has the bigger one” contest storyline was silly and stupid. Sorry, but it was. <br><br>2. I really squirmed at the portrayal of Lex. This is Lex “other than Darkseid and the Joker, I’m the coolest, most diabolical bad guy in the history of DC badguyness” Luthor. He came across in this story as lame, insignificant and petty. That is, until the last page of issue 5 when he finally came through like Lex should. Still, too little too late. Lex deserves better. <br><br>3. The black kryptonite story...Hells NO...and no again...bad idea...nuff said. <br><br>Now Jimmy Olsen in a bra was pretty damn funny. However, the rest of the portrayal of Jimmy, in the aforementioned Black Kryptonite episode, was just hokey and uninteresting. <br><br>Now, there are certainly some positive aspects to the story. I thought the first issue was good and some of the SF ideas/concepts introduced were quite clever. For example, genetically grown human suicide-bombs...nicely done. In addition, the last issue was fun and also had some real poignancy at the end. Enough that I plan to pick up the next volume in this series and see where it goes from here. <br><br>But issues two, three, four and five...MEH...didn’t much care for them. <br><br>Overall, not bad and a million times better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2239435.All_Star_Batman_and_Robin_the_Boy_Wonder__Vol__1" title="All-Star Batman and Robin the Boy Wonder, Vol. 1 by Frank Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">All-Star Batman &amp; Robin the Boy Wonder, Volume 1</a>, but I can bring myself to give it more than 2.0 to 2.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16951463065848539891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_9240637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9240637" />
    <a title="Keith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31002-keith"><img alt="Keith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471996653p2/31002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9240637?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith" href="/user/show/31002-keith">Keith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9240637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9951204791874240451">Despite the fact that I read a lot of comics -- and I do read a lot of comics -- I don't read a lot of superhero comics. Which isn't true at all, because I read a <i>lot</i> of superhero comics; it's just that almost all the superhero comics I read are Batman. I am absolutely obsessed with Batman in a way I've learned to live with, and I don't feel the need for non-comics fans or non-superhero fans to 'get it,' because so many other people obviously already do.<br/><br/>But. If, say, you were getting into comics</span>
  <span id="freeText9951204791874240451" style="display:none">Despite the fact that I read a lot of comics -- and I do read a lot of comics -- I don't read a lot of superhero comics. Which isn't true at all, because I read a <i>lot</i> of superhero comics; it's just that almost all the superhero comics I read are Batman. I am absolutely obsessed with Batman in a way I've learned to live with, and I don't feel the need for non-comics fans or non-superhero fans to 'get it,' because so many other people obviously already do.<br /><br />But. If, say, you were getting into comics -- but you were getting into them as an adult, say, and you were trying to walk that fine line that all us comic-fans walk, of enjoying the goofy weirdness that comics can bring without falling into the depressing trench of Those People Who Read Comics -- if, basically, you were trying to find that magic line where the Good meets the Terrible and Transcends...<br /><br />Well, at some point or another, you'd probably ask yourself what the hell superhero comics were all about, and if there were any part of you that could ever appreciate them, both unironically and without becoming one of Those People Who Read Comics.<br /><br />And probably, if you had friends like me who read a lot of comics and sort of openly wished they could make you see what was beautiful about them, even superhero comics...<br /><br />It would be folly to recommend Batman to you. Because Batman isn't about superhero comics. Batman is about loving Batman, and while there is a rich, dark world that lies within, you wouldn't really have that amazing staring-at-the-universe moment that superhero comics can, through their ham-fisted hopefulness, let bloom within you.<br /><br />It would be equally folly to recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/472331.Watchmen" title="Watchmen by Alan Moore" rel="nofollow noopener">Watchmen</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/160211.Zot__Book_1" title="Zot! Book 1 by Scott McCloud" rel="nofollow noopener">Zot!</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2140338.The_Starman_Omnibus__Vol__1" title="The Starman Omnibus, Vol. 1 by James Robinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Starman</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/105864.Powers__Vol__1_Who_Killed_Retro_Girl_" title="Powers, Vol. 1 Who Killed Retro Girl? by Brian Michael Bendis" rel="nofollow noopener">Powers</a>,or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/72111.Astro_City_Vol__1_Life_in_the_Big_City" title="Astro City Vol. 1 Life in the Big City by Kurt Busiek" rel="nofollow noopener">Astro City</a>, or any of the other post-modern superhero fare that gets offered up as "gateway comics" for the uninitiated, like it makes any sense at all to foster the incredulous joy of superhero comics through an analytical back door, in which the mechanics of how the genre works are stripped and enjoyed, at best, as meta-fiction. <br /><br />The aforementioned works are all brilliant in their own rights, no doubt. But that is not what superhero comics are about. These books are the works of people attempting to recover from the intense, brain-blasting heartbreak of pure emotion that superhero comics instilled in them when they were too young to know any better. These books are intellectualized post-mortems done on innocence.<br /><br />And yes -- in a way, if you are entering into comics as an adult, there will always be something you missed out on. There will always be a strange confusion in you when you see a lifelong reader's eyes glaze over with shy happiness at the sight of a single issue of <i>Fight-Man Fights Gigantor in X-World #685</i>. You both know that what lies within those pages will be silly and underwhelming and embarrassing and base...but the lifelong reader knows (and more importantly, <i>feels</i>) that a secret joy still lives here, and can't be washed away by age.<br /><br />But, throwing that hopelessness aside -- let's assume that you still demanded to know just what this fuss was all about. Let's say you insisted that the child in you could still be touched by something unabashedly resplendent, even if it was a decade or two too late.<br /><br />I'd say this.<br /><br />I'd say, "Look, a few years ago a writer and an artist who you've never heard of but who are really famous in comics -- a few years ago they teamed up and they made a Superman book. And you don't have to think Superman is cool, because <i>I</i> don't think he's very cool. And you really don't have to know anything more about it, but it's not going to feel dated or stilted or any of those things that turn you off, except when it does so in very charming ways. And it's short -- only a couple paperbacks.<br /><br />And this book. I mean, I don't want to spoil it for you by explaining it. But this book, I think, will help you <i>get it</i>."<br /><br />That is what I would say to you. <i>That</i> is what I would say.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9951204791874240451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_226800990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226800990" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226800990?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=superhumans">superhumans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226800990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11808052306664201672">Dear Grant Morrison,<br/><br/>It's not you, it's me. I should have known better. I've never been a big fan of Superman. We both know that I'm much more of a Batman sort of girl. I can't think of a single Superman book that I've loved. I probably should have left well enough alone. But I was curious, and anything had to be better than Frank Miller's All-Star Batman. That much was true. At least you seem to understand Superman's character, in a way that Miller no longer understands Batman's and has never un</span>
  <span id="freeText11808052306664201672" style="display:none">Dear Grant Morrison,<br /><br />It's not you, it's me. I should have known better. I've never been a big fan of Superman. We both know that I'm much more of a Batman sort of girl. I can't think of a single Superman book that I've loved. I probably should have left well enough alone. But I was curious, and anything had to be better than Frank Miller's All-Star Batman. That much was true. At least you seem to understand Superman's character, in a way that Miller no longer understands Batman's and has never understood Superman's. You know that the core of him is defined by Ma and Pa Kent. I can respect that. There's so much temptation to make things darker and edgier, and you withstood much of that. And we all know that you're a writer with no problem going to the dark side. And I have to thank you, from the bottom of my heart, for not writing your female characters as sex objects.<br /><br />That's the good part. But I thought the point of these All-Star books was supposed to be in presenting these iconic characters without all of the backstory getting in the way. But it felt like a lot of backstory was floating around here, and not being well-versed in Superlore, I felt lost half the time. Like, who the hell is Samson? I'm still not sure. I'm pretty sure I don't want to know. He wasn't exactly engaging while he was onstage. In fact, most of the individual storylines were less than compelling. The overarching storyline, about Superman facing death, was actually quite interesting. Maybe a bit more of that and a bit less of Lois's birthday superpowers. <br /><br />It all felt very retro, in a way, right down to Superman's Girlfriend Lois Lane getting superpowers for a day. I think I remember seeing a story like that from back in the Silver Age. The whole thing felt Silver Age. But that's not really my thing, so it didn't work for me. Again, it's not you, it's me. I'm sure there are plenty of readers who adore Silver Age stylings, and they'd be right at home here. <br /><br />Also, could you tell Frank Quitely that Superman gave up the donuts long ago? I know that's his style, but everybody just looks so round. So much like the plush toy versions. It looks odd, especially on Superman. Can't say I'm a fan of that.<br /><br />With polite indifference,<br />Sesana</span>
  <a data-text-id="11808052306664201672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2062796622" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2062796622" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2062796622?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Superman fans!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=best-of-2017">best-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-hero">strong-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=dc-comics">dc-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=grant-morrison">grant-morrison</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=young-adult-teen-books">young-adult-teen-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062796622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6141760212248581837"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500271391i/23316024._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='Superman' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>5.5 stars!!!</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Introduction: </u>
</b><br/><br/>Now, I have a little confession to make (I seem to be making so many book confessions lately, right)? I had only read a few “Superman” comics over the years, which included “Superman: Whatever Happened to the Man of Tomorrow” and “Superman: Secret Identity.” The reason why I have not read that many “Superman” comics was not because I hate Superman (I actually really like his character), but it was hard for me to look for some recommendations for good “Superman” </span>
  <span id="freeText6141760212248581837" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500271391i/23316024._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="Superman" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>5.5 stars!!!</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Introduction: </u>
</b><br><br>Now, I have a little confession to make (I seem to be making so many book confessions lately, right)? I had only read a few “Superman” comics over the years, which included “Superman: Whatever Happened to the Man of Tomorrow” and “Superman: Secret Identity.” The reason why I have not read that many “Superman” comics was not because I hate Superman (I actually really like his character), but it was hard for me to look for some recommendations for good “Superman” stories while recommendations for good “Batman” stories came much more readily. One of the “Superman” stories that was always highly recommended to me was Grant Morrison’s run on “Superman” called “All-Star Superman.” At first, I was a bit hesitant about checking this series out because from what I had heard from some comic book fans, Grant Morrison’s works tend to jump off the deep end at a certain point in his stories and I had experienced that with his work on “Batman R.I.P.” However, after I finally decided to dive into this graphic novel, I now see why this particular graphic novel was so highly recommended to me and I have to say that “All-Star Superman Volume One” is one of the best “Superman” stories I had ever read!<br><br><b>
  <u>What is this story about?</u>
</b><br><br>The story starts off with Superman going to the sun to rescue a space crew who were on a mission to take fire from the sun and it turns out that because Superman went too near the sun, he contracted apoptosis, death of the body cells, which means that he will soon die. When Superman finds this out, he decides that he must do some things on Earth before he dies, such as temporarily giving his love interest Lois Lane superpowers for her birthday and trying to confess his secret identity to her, getting in a fight with Jimmy Olsen due to being affected by Black Kryptonite, meeting up with his nemesis Lex Luthor, and saying his goodbyes to his father Jonathan Kent.<br><br><b>
  <i>Will Superman have time to do all of these things before he dies?<br><br>Read this graphic novel to find out!</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>What I loved about this story:</u>
</b><br><br><u>Grant Morrison’s writing:</u> I really enjoyed Grant Morrison’s writing in this graphic novel as the story has a nice mixture of drama and humor thrown in and I often found myself laughing at some of the situations in this volume, such as Superman and Lois’ encounter with the comical superhero duo Samson and Atlas. I also like the fact that this story tackles the subject about what would happen if Superman is about to die and how he would spend his last days on Earth (although, the concept about Superman dying is nothing new at this point). This gives Grant Morrison a chance to explore Superman’s life from his arrival to Earth and being adopted by Jonathan and Martha Kent to working in the Daily Planet and meeting Lois Lane and there is a great love to the character as not only do older readers get to see Superman’s life be presented again in this volume, but new readers will be able to understand more about Superman’s origins through a modern interpretation. I also enjoyed the way that Grant Morrison portrayed Superman in this volume as Superman is not shown as being a flat character, but has many dimensions to his personality as we get to see Superman become sad, happy, angry and humorous all at once in this volume; it was fantastic seeing the various emotions that Superman displays in this volume contribute to the story at hand.<br><br><u>Frank Quitely’s artwork:</u> While there are some parts of Frank Quitely’s artwork that annoyed me a bit, which I will discuss more about in the cons section, overall, the artwork is extremely detailed and gorgeous to look at. Probably my most favorite image in this graphic novel was the image of Superman and Lois Lane kissing each other on the moon and you can see the gorgeous detail being done to Lois’ wavy hair as it is waving around in space.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1500271391i/23316023._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="Superman" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>
  <u>What made me feel uncomfortable about this story:</u>
</b><br><br>The only problem I have with this graphic novel is that there are so many things happening in the story that it would make it pretty confusing for anyone who is not used to reading “Superman” comics. Even though I found this graphic novel to be pretty entertaining, the narrative can get overcrowded at times because there are so many events going on and you have to read each issue a bit carefully to get the full details of each of the stories. Also, some of the artwork can be a bit off at times, especially with the way that Superman’s face seems to look like dough in some panels and I felt that he was drawn a bit too bulky in this volume, despite the fact that Superman is naturally muscular.<br><br><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts:</u>
</b><br><br>Overall, “All-Star Superman Volume One” is seriously one fantastic and hilarious volume that I would love to read over and over again if I get the chance to and I cannot wait to read the second volume of this series!<br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2017/07/all-star-superman-volume-1-by-grant.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406978887i/10622960._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="Banner" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6141760212248581837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_252412321" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252412321" />
    <a title="Rhiannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5071150-rhiannon"><img alt="Rhiannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302016584p2/5071150.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252412321?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhiannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhiannon" href="/user/show/5071150-rhiannon">Rhiannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401211028" href="/book/show/2325421.All_Star_Superman">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who think they don't care about Superman</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5071150-rhiannon?shelf=spaaaace">spaaaace</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252412321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5809336401187663044">Look! Superman playing super-fetch with his super-dog! Aw!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365781i/717935.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Hey, guys. Guess what I read yesterday? Superman. Isn't that weird? <br/><br/>Well, it was "Buy 1 Graphic Novel, Get 1 For $1" Day @ my work. And I had stocked up on the latest volumes of the three series that I am currently in the middle of (Fables, The Walking Dead, Chew). I just needed one more! And the stock was looking slim (yay! sales; boo! none for me). When this guy that I work with, Tyler, hands me Grant Morrison's All-Star Superman. Since</span>
  <span id="freeText5809336401187663044" style="display:none">Look! Superman playing super-fetch with his super-dog! Aw!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365781i/717935.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Hey, guys. Guess what I read yesterday? Superman. Isn't that weird? <br><br>Well, it was "Buy 1 Graphic Novel, Get 1 For $1" Day @ my work. And I had stocked up on the latest volumes of the three series that I am currently in the middle of (Fables, The Walking Dead, Chew). I just needed one more! And the stock was looking slim (yay! sales; boo! none for me). When this guy that I work with, Tyler, hands me Grant Morrison's All-Star Superman. Since he knows what he's talking about when it comes to superhero comics - and I certainly don't - I bit. <br><br>Now, I have a "working knowledge" of Grant Morrison, since I compose the company's weekly Comic Book newsletter. He's like a big deal guy that everyone lurves. And I have the same ingrained "because- you're-an-American" pop culture knowledge of Superman that you probably have... you know: Krypton, Clark Kent, Phonebooths, Lois Lane, Smallville, Lex Luthor... that kind of thing. But, I had never wanted to read a Superman comic before. And I'd never seen a Superman movie or television show. I just figured I knew all I wanted to know about Superman. <br><br>But, this was really, really good!<br><br>Frank Quitely does the artwork, and man! His Clark Kent is fucking adorable. He's goofy and clumsy and chubby (!) and sweet. Look at this guy: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365781i/717936.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Aw! Pigeon-toed? Cute. <br><br>The storyline goes like this: Superman goes to save some dummies who are flying into the sun, and gets Superman-Cancer. Ordinarily, the Sun gives Superman all kinds of awesome powers, but THIS TIME, he overdid it, and now his cells are so bursting with power that they are going to overload. Of course, Lex Luthor sent those dummies into the sun in the first place, knowing Superman would save them (and the world), and hence - Lex Luthor is responsible for Superman's impending death. Mwah-ha-ha-ha-ha. <br><br>For the most part, the rest of the comic revolves around Superman coming to terms with his death, preparing the world for a Superman-less future, and trying to convince Lois Lane that he's been Clark Kent all along (she doesn't believe him...). <br><br>It's actually really touching! <br><br>One of the things that I enjoyed about Morrison's story is that I didn't necessarily have to know too much about Superman besides the mythos, you know? There are references to events that have taken place throughout the evolving Superman stories, but nothing Morrison couldn't explain to me in a non-condescending way. And, I do not know for sure (this is just a guess), but I think Morrison really added some arcane bits of Superman's past for the real fans, too. <br><br>Anyways, the reason I docked this book a star is that while this was a really great read, a couple of things were kind of dumb. <br><br>1. Superman gives Lois Lane Superman-powers for a day as a gift. This would've been a really fun little episode to read, except some asshole characters (Samson, Atlas) stepped out of the space-time-continuum, or whatever, and started harping on Lois Lane and ruined it. The two dudes and Superman get into a dick-measuring contest over who can "win" Lois, and she just poses for the entire length of the chapter instead of doing anything interesting. Srsly? So lame. What year is it? 1940? This part was a sexist PoS... <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365781i/717937.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2. Superman gets exposed to "black kryptonite" and turns "bad" for a few pages. But, something also impairs his mental functions during this time, so he's also a bit retarded or something. I don't know. The dialogue took a turn for the INANE, and I was left laughing at what could've been a dramatic moment. It was so silly. In a bad way. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365781i/717938.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>3. That Superman chin? It was out of fucking control. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365781i/717939.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">￼ <br><br>But, other than that chin and stuff - this first volume of All-Star Superman was actually very enjoyable, and I will definitely be reading the second volume in the series soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5809336401187663044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText16311300605810943720" style="display:none">I've had this Comic for *ages* without reading it-&amp; I should've read it sooner, as it's really good. :)<br />The storylines for each episode are all different, yet often interlinking &amp; all of the usual suspects in terms of characters are in it. <br />The artworks nice-Retro mixed with modern with a good amount of detail when needed.<br />However, what let it down a bit for me was the way that Clark Kent/Superman himself was drawn sometimes. <div id="review_40082250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40082250" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1409476-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474063444p2/1409476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40082250?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/1409476-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40082250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5809377381732833248">Morrison is a great comic book writer, but he has a few obvious flaws that can make his work difficult to digest, and have always kept him from reaching the same heights as Alan Moore.<br/><br/>All-Star Superman, while using the same deconstructed narrative and mind-blowingly bizarre gift of invention that are his trademarks, manages to overcome those limitations and essentially create the platonic ideal of what a Superman story should be.<br/><br/>In twelve issues this series manages to truly show how an epic stor</span>
  <span id="freeText5809377381732833248" style="display:none">Morrison is a great comic book writer, but he has a few obvious flaws that can make his work difficult to digest, and have always kept him from reaching the same heights as Alan Moore.<br /><br />All-Star Superman, while using the same deconstructed narrative and mind-blowingly bizarre gift of invention that are his trademarks, manages to overcome those limitations and essentially create the platonic ideal of what a Superman story should be.<br /><br />In twelve issues this series manages to truly show how an epic story can be told about a man who cannot be hurt by normal means. It throws us into a universe that is already deep and rich, and where this hero has been that planet's protector for many years. It unflinchingly goes from silly to hardcore sci-fi, all with a strong emotional undercurrent that drives everything forward.<br /><br />It's not perfect, and I still found myself wondering what the hell he was talking about from time to time, but the whole is far greater than the sum of its parts. And with his background in the occult and kabbalistic magick, Morrison manages to take Superman beyond just being a simple Christ figure.<br /><br />I read someone describe this as is the "only Superman story you'll ever need" and they're probably right.<br /><br />Note that you'll need to read both volumes to get the full story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5809377381732833248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review40082250">

<div id="review_811087077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/811087077" />
    <a title="Chantaal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279192-chantaal"><img alt="Chantaal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529987921p2/279192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/811087077?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantaal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantaal" href="/user/show/279192-chantaal">Chantaal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401211028" href="/book/show/2325421.All_Star_Superman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279192-chantaal?shelf=comics-graphic-novels-manga">comics-graphic-novels-manga</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer811087077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16423302798027820965">I keep wanting to like Superman, to find those epic stories that boil him down to the essentials and show why people love him so much. All-Star Superman was one recommended to me, and I came away with nothing but meh. <br/><br/>Most of this feels so over the top and hokey (Black kryptonite? Jimmy Olsen what are you doing? Atlas and Sampson's pissing match over Lois, let me puke), which only buries the nicer moments.<br/><br/>Also, I have never, ever liked Quitely's art. Too many potato faces and giant bodybuilder n</span>
  <span id="freeText16423302798027820965" style="display:none">I keep wanting to like Superman, to find those epic stories that boil him down to the essentials and show why people love him so much. All-Star Superman was one recommended to me, and I came away with nothing but meh. <br /><br />Most of this feels so over the top and hokey (Black kryptonite? Jimmy Olsen what are you doing? Atlas and Sampson's pissing match over Lois, let me puke), which only buries the nicer moments.<br /><br />Also, I have never, ever liked Quitely's art. Too many potato faces and giant bodybuilder necks. Why the neck as thick as his head, Quitely? WHY?<br /><br />I won't be moving on to volume two, unless someone can give me an incredibly compelling reason to. And if you know of any other Superman stories I should be reading, please share, I will happily check them out. One day I will understand Superman. One day. </span>

<div id="review_205392334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205392334" />
    <a title="Cameron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3372450-cameron"><img alt="Cameron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267923914p2/3372450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205392334?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cameron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cameron" href="/user/show/3372450-cameron">Cameron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3372450-cameron?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3372450-cameron?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205392334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2422727961731756541">Let it not be said that throughout my history of reading comics I have not given Superman and his creative teams ample opportunity to make me a fan. Because I have. Probably more opportunity than both my free time and my wallet really appreciate, to be honest. This persistent (and futile, I now realize), pursuit of the Man of Steel's fandom was most likely fueled by a few fleeting moments of brilliance in stories about him I've read in the past. (Those stories being <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373150.It_s_a_Bird___' title='It's a Bird... by Steven T. Seagle' rel='nofollow noopener'>It's a Bird...</a> by Steven T. S</span>
  <span id="freeText2422727961731756541" style="display:none">Let it not be said that throughout my history of reading comics I have not given Superman and his creative teams ample opportunity to make me a fan. Because I have. Probably more opportunity than both my free time and my wallet really appreciate, to be honest. This persistent (and futile, I now realize), pursuit of the Man of Steel's fandom was most likely fueled by a few fleeting moments of brilliance in stories about him I've read in the past. (Those stories being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373150.It_s_a_Bird___" title="It's a Bird... by Steven T. Seagle" rel="nofollow noopener">It's a Bird...</a> by Steven T. Seagle and a short story called "Life Support" written by Damon Lindelof that appeared in Action Comics #900 and was absolutely brilliant.) The only problem with those stories were the fact that, while each story dealt directly with Superman, neither of them actually prominently featured him. So, in a last ditch effort to find value of some sort in the character, I turned to Grant Morrison and Frank Quitely, authors of the decently emotionally affecting We3. I now think that was a mistake.<br /><br />Quitely is a pretty awesome artist, but I'm glad I was introduced to his pencil work through another book, as his work here is uncharacteristically bad. Proportions, especially of the facial variety, seem incredibly off to me. This mismatching extends to the physique of many of the characters as well, Superman most notably. And while I'm willing to forgive that Supes' bodily proportions don't necessarily have to be normal (he isn't human, after all), his disproportionate body doesn't look like alien physiology, it looks like bad artistry.<br /><br />The stunning and memorable panels and visual techniques employed in other works of Frank Quitely (such as the aforementioned We3) are completely absent here, which is highly disappointing. There's nothing special about the presentation here, and while I don't mean to say that standard delivery can't be effective, I was really hoping to see more of Quitely's creative visual style. Perhaps I've been spoiled when it comes to him.<br /><br />On the writing side of things, Grant Morrison's writing, much as I hate to say it, is frustratingly stupid and amateurish. The stories in this volume are often ridiculous, even by superhero standards, though not because they're outlandish. Instead, it's because things like common sense are ignored where it's consideration would make the story collapse and the out of nowhere revelations at the end of stories that explain everything with a hand wave Harry Potter style.<br /><br />Morrison's writing isn't entirely bad though. He shows shades of his talent in a few scenes involving Lex Luthor, a character many times more interesting than the star of the show. It's a shame, then, that we spend such little time with him. Instead we spend most of the comic with a boring protagonist and a good portion of it with an annoyingly stubborn Lois Lane.<br /><br />Perhaps I would have a different point of view had I entered into this book with the mentality of a fan. I'm certain I've enjoyed some stories more than they may have objectively deserved when Spider-Man was the central focus due to my fondness for the cast and mythology of the character. Perhaps that's the key to enjoying this volume. Fans of Superman may very well enjoy the hell out of this. For this non-fan, however, the story was overwhelmingly dumb and not worth the effort.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2422727961731756541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_916817956" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916817956" />
    <a title="Yvonne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30741137-yvonne"><img alt="Yvonne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398120410p2/30741137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/916817956?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yvonne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yvonne" href="/user/show/30741137-yvonne">Yvonne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30741137-yvonne?shelf=superhero-books">superhero-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30741137-yvonne?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30741137-yvonne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30741137-yvonne?shelf=its-a-picture-book">its-a-picture-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30741137-yvonne?shelf=fanfiction-sometimes-glorified">fanfiction-sometimes-glorified</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30741137-yvonne?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer916817956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2744839020560764801">I honestly don’t know what to think of this now that I have read it. I was fun, it was colorful and brilliant, and yet overall it didn’t make much sense to me. It’s like when they sat down to write this superman book they decided to explore x number of stories and themes and in the end all those themes and stories didn’t flow with each other in the amount of allotted pages they were given. <br/><br/>Here’s the gist of what I saw in this book. <br/><br/>Superman is dying by the hands of Luthor. <br/><br/>Luthor is okay with g</span>
  <span id="freeText2744839020560764801" style="display:none">I honestly don’t know what to think of this now that I have read it. I was fun, it was colorful and brilliant, and yet overall it didn’t make much sense to me. It’s like when they sat down to write this superman book they decided to explore x number of stories and themes and in the end all those themes and stories didn’t flow with each other in the amount of allotted pages they were given. <br /><br />Here’s the gist of what I saw in this book. <br /><br />Superman is dying by the hands of Luthor. <br /><br />Luthor is okay with going to his death because he 'killed' Superman. <br /><br />Lois Lanes Birthday. <br /><br />A day in the life of Jimmy Olsen, who, at the time, is experiencing a day in the life of another person’s life. <br /><br />A retelling of the death of Pa Kent. This one always gets me. Prepare to see me well up with tears folks. (The only time I didn’t get the feels for Pa was when he got knocked off in the first Henry Cavil Superman movie. I don’t care how much you love your dog, leave the poor thing to die if there’s a chance YOU won’t make it back alive.) <br /><br />And Superman’s offspring/time travel. <br /><br />Overall the book gave me the impression that I was looking at an older Superman story telling of the 1960’s, as if we had never given up that strange and whimsical way of writing comic books, but our writing style has evolved all the same. If that were the case then I would say we saw an issue of Action Comics, Superman’s Girl friend Lois Lane, Superman’s Pal Jimmy Olsen, Superman and an issue of Superboy. <br /><br />I guess if I look at it that way I could say I got five different superman stories with only a little bit of overlap of plot in each one. This was fun, but if you want something a little more coherent this isn’t for you. Probably not the best book for someone just beginning to explore Superman either, but if you really like the big lug you might give this a try. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2744839020560764801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer7571302023084794136">Too much hard to follow techno-jurgons and incomprehensible weird sci-fi elements to enjoy the Superman-adventures properly, and all the episodes felt rather disjointed and scattered instead of a firmly connected chronological development of a single plot. Still, independently, the plots of each of the episodes works, even though they were not very interesting (other than Superman slowly dying and finally revealed his trueself to Lois so that they can spend some quality time together, which was </span>
  <span id="freeText7571302023084794136" style="display:none">Too much hard to follow techno-jurgons and incomprehensible weird sci-fi elements to enjoy the Superman-adventures properly, and all the episodes felt rather disjointed and scattered instead of a firmly connected chronological development of a single plot. Still, independently, the plots of each of the episodes works, even though they were not very interesting (other than Superman slowly dying and finally revealed his trueself to Lois so that they can spend some quality time together, which was fun). But the characterizations were much more up to the mark than the plots and in the short span of each episodes they worked perfectly, detailing classic supporting characters like Lex Luthor, Lois Lane and Jimmy Olsen's true motivations and inner driving forces, and of course Superman himself. All in all, a good read, but not a great one as I was hoping for.<br /><br />Update: After finishing the whole <i>All-Star Superman</i>, I can now see with a clearer eye how Morrison built the foundation through these earlier seemingly unconnected storylines which turned into one (more of less) cohesive complete storyarc connecting most of them by the end. So in retrospect, even though I didn't enjoy this volume that much, or at least nowhere near as much as the next volume, I had to view everything in a new light, and decided it deserves another star with my original three stars (more like 3.5 actually).</span>
  <a data-text-id="7571302023084794136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_604891384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/604891384" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4598314-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391090778p2/4598314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/604891384?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/4598314-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=comics-manga">comics-manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer604891384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16417672023982545254">Poor Superman is always going to start off on the wrong foot with me, and having him written by Grant Morrison doesn't make things much better. Fortunately, I've read Morrison's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22358.We3' title='We3 by Grant Morrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>We3</a>, where he lets Quitely's art do what it's supposed to do: tell the story--so I expected to see as much here. Secondly, Morrison's approach to this series pleased me, as he stated in the planning stages, that he did not want to rehash Superman's origin story, yet again. The point of All-Star Superman is to give us the</span>
  <span id="freeText16417672023982545254" style="display:none">Poor Superman is always going to start off on the wrong foot with me, and having him written by Grant Morrison doesn't make things much better. Fortunately, I've read Morrison's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22358.We3" title="We3 by Grant Morrison" rel="nofollow noopener">We3</a>, where he lets Quitely's art do what it's supposed to do: tell the story--so I expected to see as much here. Secondly, Morrison's approach to this series pleased me, as he stated in the planning stages, that he did not want to rehash Superman's origin story, yet again. The point of All-Star Superman is to give us the essence of the character, which is what I have been looking for all this time.<br /><br />Superman fans who have seen my low ratings of other tales such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8172.Superman_Birthright" title="Superman Birthright by Mark Waid" rel="nofollow noopener">Superman: Birthright</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7657484.Superman_Earth_One" title="Superman Earth One by J. Michael Straczynski" rel="nofollow noopener">Superman: Earth One</a>, while I praise alternate, darker visions of the characters like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/154798.Superman_Red_Son" title="Superman Red Son by Mark Millar" rel="nofollow noopener">Superman: Red Son</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/401200.Lex_Luthor_Man_of_Steel" title="Lex Luthor Man of Steel by Brian Azzarello" rel="nofollow noopener">Lex Luthor: Man of Steel</a>, probably think I'm trolling. What I have been doing in my readings is try to understand why people like this character that just doesn't make sense to me. He's a god disguising himself as a human. That's not fitting in. That's just damn good acting. "But you read stories about people who command the weather and shoot laser beams out of their eyes," people argue. I sure do, but for me, the X-Men have always been human beings first. The world as a whole might hate them from time to time, but the X-stories have always given the mutants a place to belong within their own community, whether it be in Xavier's mansion, or in the sewers with the Morlocks. They always have a place where they can be themselves. Meanwhile, Superman fans have tried to convince me that Kal'El is the very same. Certainly he wants that, but how can he ever have that when he is completely alien? Yes, he has moments of weakness thanks to kryptonite where he gets to experience life as a weak little human being for a few days, but he always gets his powers back so he can save the day. That's not quite a mile in my shoes, Clark.<br /><br />But All-Star Superman addresses many of my concerns, sometimes in very amusing ways. Most notably, the concept of no one recognizing Clark as Superman. I like that Morrison and Quitely actually change his physical appearance beyond hair and glasses. Here, Clark is a little bit overweight, to go along with his cowardly, clutzy demeanor. And when he reveals himself to Lois, the Pulitzer prize winning investigative report, and even Lex, the most brilliant mind in the world, no one can fathom that they are one and the same, even if there is a striking resemblance. I love the way Morrison/Quitely really play up the concept of mind over matter, letting even the most intuitive minds only see what they want to see. <br /><br />All-Star Superman tells the story of a dying hero who has ironically being killed by the very thing that gives him his power: the sun. <br /><br />I keep saying that I want a well-written Superman story that helps me to appreciate the character, even though I may never like him. This is it. In fact, it is the Superman story I should have read first and just skipped all of these origin stories that try to tell a "new" story despite being forever forced into the Superman standards of Daily Planet, Krypton, Ma and Pa Kent, Lois Lane, Lex Luthor, etc etc. By shedding the need for these chains, while still working on the assumption that I am fully aware of them, Morrison/Quitely just give me a look at the Man of Steel. The lonely man who is loved and hated by those around him, and appreciates that, but knows he can never be one of them. Morrison and Quitely aren't asking me to love him too, or even respect him. They are just presenting him as he is and it's up to me to take him or leave him.<br /><br />At the end of the day, I don't like the character, but I can accept this "just shut up and Superman" story as a fine example of who and what he is. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.BiblioSanctum.com">www.BiblioSanctum.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16417672023982545254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1638940996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638940996" />
    <a title="DeAnna Knippling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3166570-deanna-knippling"><img alt="DeAnna Knippling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442526565p2/3166570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638940996?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeAnna Knippling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeAnna Knippling" href="/user/show/3166570-deanna-knippling">DeAnna Knippling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3166570-deanna-knippling?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638940996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16040927843449957078">I have a friend who's trying to convince me that I'm giving short shrift to Supes over...a lot of other superhero characters. This despite the fact that I am, to those who know me, more of a horror/noir/crime reader. I don't *love* uplifting stories. I barely *like* them, unless the uplift comes up out of some verifiable muck. The one Supes story that I *love* is the Judd Winick story, Superman/Shazam: First Thunder--which fits the bill exactly, IMO.<br/><br/>So I can't say that I *love* this book. It was</span>
  <span id="freeText16040927843449957078" style="display:none">I have a friend who's trying to convince me that I'm giving short shrift to Supes over...a lot of other superhero characters. This despite the fact that I am, to those who know me, more of a horror/noir/crime reader. I don't *love* uplifting stories. I barely *like* them, unless the uplift comes up out of some verifiable muck. The one Supes story that I *love* is the Judd Winick story, Superman/Shazam: First Thunder--which fits the bill exactly, IMO.<br /><br />So I can't say that I *love* this book. It was all right. In fact it was a bit cheesy for me, or rather the wrong kind of cheesy for me. I didn't care for the art and I thought the plots were meh (and insulting toward Lois SHE IS NOT AN IDIOT and saying she isn't an idiot and then making her act like one just tells me that this comic was never meant for me). </span>
  <a data-text-id="16040927843449957078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_931523702" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931523702" />
    <a title="Ville-markus Nevalainen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28393319-ville-markus-nevalainen"><img alt="Ville-markus Nevalainen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450300931p2/28393319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/931523702?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ville-markus Nevalainen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ville-markus Nevalainen" href="/user/show/28393319-ville-markus-nevalainen">Ville-markus Nevalainen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer931523702" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17109401153994132712">All-Star Superman is a comic that I had heard lot about. Many have said that it is The Superman comic that you should read, and how can you argue with a name like All-Star Superman?<br/><br/>But after reading it... I hope this is not the best Superman can do. The story is a complete mess as is the art style. All-Star Superman is an example of how the universe behind the characters have grown too large for a new reader to understand it. I, who vaguely knows who Jimmy Olsen is, found myself confused from ti</span>
  <span id="freeText17109401153994132712" style="display:none">All-Star Superman is a comic that I had heard lot about. Many have said that it is The Superman comic that you should read, and how can you argue with a name like All-Star Superman?<br /><br />But after reading it... I hope this is not the best Superman can do. The story is a complete mess as is the art style. All-Star Superman is an example of how the universe behind the characters have grown too large for a new reader to understand it. I, who vaguely knows who Jimmy Olsen is, found myself confused from time and time again. There are lot of characters who are not introduced but just shoved to the story, then to dissappear next chapter.<br /><br />The story starts with Superman saving bunch of scientists going in the... sun? And inside the shuttle there's "genetically modified suicide bomb in human form". And the creature says that out loud. So Superman flies to save the day, but in the process he has absorbed too much energy and now he's dying.<br /><br />The second chapter delves a bit more in this problem, but after that it's just scene after scene nothing making any sense, not alone or together.<br /><br />In the end it's difficult to say what the story is about. There's Lex Luthor, Lois, future Supermen, dinosaurmen, gods and timetravellers. So much and at the same time, so little.<br /><br />What surprised me was the amount of science fiction in the story. It made the story even more difficult to follow, but it also made it more unbelievable. I certainly didn't know how futuristic Superman stories were, and I found myself almost laughing in disbelief. Is this actually happening, I wondered. The scientists love to ramble with long words, but like everything else, this doesnt make a lot of sense or has any meaning.<br /><br />Unfortunately even the art can't make up for the mistakes in the story. In a way the art represents the story quite well: it's inconsistent, empty and at the same time the characters are built to look like model men and women. It's not just Superman's huge, square jaw or his suit, but everything. There's a feeling that this isn't truly happening, it's always few steps away from you, there's no real emotion. Still, the most irritating part maybe the fact that the characters look like different persons in different pictures.<br /><br />I really can't recommend All-Star Superman, not atleast for those who are just discovering Superman comics. And even if you were familiar with the setting and the characters, I doubt the story would turn to anything great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17109401153994132712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_694381678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/694381678" />
    <a title="Jay Becker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10698831-jay-becker"><img alt="Jay Becker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578955818p2/10698831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/694381678?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay Becker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay Becker" href="/user/show/10698831-jay-becker">Jay Becker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694381678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12953733275533583312">This is one of the better comics I have read in quite some time. Morrison can get pretty heady sometimes but this is really a love story to the Silver Age Superman. Sort of like Moore's "Whatever happened to the Man of Tomorrow" it takes all the crazy silver age stuff (the key to the fortress, Jimmy Olsen's signal watch and crazy identities, etc, etc, etc) and turns it on it's head and makes it work. Quitely's artwork while hard to call pretty is extremely effective. His Clark Kent is AMAZING an</span>
  <span id="freeText12953733275533583312" style="display:none">This is one of the better comics I have read in quite some time. Morrison can get pretty heady sometimes but this is really a love story to the Silver Age Superman. Sort of like Moore's "Whatever happened to the Man of Tomorrow" it takes all the crazy silver age stuff (the key to the fortress, Jimmy Olsen's signal watch and crazy identities, etc, etc, etc) and turns it on it's head and makes it work. Quitely's artwork while hard to call pretty is extremely effective. His Clark Kent is AMAZING and you can truly believe that no one would think he is Superman. Add in a truly terrifying Luthor and you have a great comic. This story contains so much of what I want from the Man of Steel and what was so lacking in "Man Of Steel."</span>
  <a data-text-id="12953733275533583312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
