<div id="review_2522471188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2522471188" />
    <a title="Ben Shee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22779311-ben-shee"><img alt="Ben Shee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375533307p2/22779311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2522471188?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Shee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Shee" href="/user/show/22779311-ben-shee">Ben Shee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2522471188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1915653746101568594">Superman, hey? <br/><br/>There was a time when I didn't care that much for Superman. He wasn't that interesting - he was invulnerable - all his modern movies are garbage.<br/><br/>This is a much better Superman story than any of the modern Superman movies. Perhaps what made Superman boring was his invulnerability, and Grant Morrison's Superman - still powerful, but weakening, makes Superman all the more brave, noble and lovable. <br/><br/>The series has some beautiful moments, as well as quite a few hilarious Clark Kent mome</span>
  <span id="freeText1915653746101568594" style="display:none">Superman, hey? <br /><br />There was a time when I didn't care that much for Superman. He wasn't that interesting - he was invulnerable - all his modern movies are garbage.<br /><br />This is a much better Superman story than any of the modern Superman movies. Perhaps what made Superman boring was his invulnerability, and Grant Morrison's Superman - still powerful, but weakening, makes Superman all the more brave, noble and lovable. <br /><br />The series has some beautiful moments, as well as quite a few hilarious Clark Kent moments. One of the things that often bothers me when it comes to heroes like Flash and Superman is the idea that they should never be able to rest, aren't crimes and unpleasant things always happening somewhere in the world? Instead they tend to act like governments of a particular city - preserving mainly that city and no others. It does conflict a little with the morality issue, though. But this is not the book to consider that - perhaps Kingdom Come is a better platform for that topic.<br /><br />There is much more to the series of course - it is intended to help us feel hope as against our society's failings <a href="https://www.newsarama.com/1445-all-star-memories-grant-morrison-on-all-star-superman-10.html" rel="nofollow noopener">(see here)</a> - although it is a bit more subtle in its criticism. A superman that hugs suicide jumpers, who misses his dad trying to save the world - a superman who is saving people (including his killer and nemesis) even as he pretends to stumble around as Clark Kent, reporting to his boss. A Superman that values science, trust and intellect - alongside hard work and sacrifice. <br /><br />There is a lot to admire in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1915653746101568594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3498273128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3498273128" />
    <a title="Dustin Johnston (dragonarmybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6291823-dustin-johnston-dragonarmybooks"><img alt="Dustin Johnston (dragonarmybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342389966p2/6291823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3498273128?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dustin Johnston (dragonarmybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dustin Johnston (dragonarmybooks)" href="/user/show/6291823-dustin-johnston-dragonarmybooks">Dustin Johnston (dragonarmybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6291823-dustin-johnston-dragonarmybooks?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6291823-dustin-johnston-dragonarmybooks?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6291823-dustin-johnston-dragonarmybooks?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3498273128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2783989504052116466">I've got some mixed feelings on this one.<br/><br/>On the one hand, I really did enjoy the illustrations and characterizations. Almost every frame is worth looking at and admiring. The amount of color and detail on every page is mesmerizing. I also love the unique care and attention the creators took in making old characters feel new, modern, and accessible. Jimmy Olsen, for example, is no longer the buffoon that no one really likes, to a real friend of Superman's that helps save both people and the world</span>
  <span id="freeText2783989504052116466" style="display:none">I've got some mixed feelings on this one.<br /><br />On the one hand, I really did enjoy the illustrations and characterizations. Almost every frame is worth looking at and admiring. The amount of color and detail on every page is mesmerizing. I also love the unique care and attention the creators took in making old characters feel new, modern, and accessible. Jimmy Olsen, for example, is no longer the buffoon that no one really likes, to a real friend of Superman's that helps save both people and the world on numerous occasions. And how they dealt with Superman v. Clark Kent was brilliant. Instead of simply giving Clark glasses and a new hairstyle, the illustrator, Frank Quitely, drew Clark hunched over, gut out, shoulders rolled forward, giving him a clumsy persona that brilliantly distinguishes between the hero and the reporter. It's so obvious but I've never seen it done this well before!<br /><br />All of those good things being said, both the stories and dialogue lacked, which is unfortunate because these are two extremely important parts, even when it comes to comics. The stories seemed rushed and incomplete. The dialogue was odd and often felt cheesy. There was very little emotion behind the stories being told. <br /><br />This is all unfortunate. While it is still a graphic novel I would suggest to some enthusiasts, it will not be one that goes on the shelf with my favorites.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2783989504052116466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756652612?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mateusz Swietoslawski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mateusz Swietoslawski" href="/user/show/55219234-mateusz-swietoslawski">Mateusz Swietoslawski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756652612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5782651683029316728"><a href='https://mateuszcelestyn.wordpress.com/2016/12/03/all-star-superman-vol-1-by-grant-morrison-w-and-frank-quitely-a/' rel='nofollow noopener'>You can check out this and my other reviews here :)</a><br/><br/>I have a theory explaining why good old Superman is so disliked nowadays. Almost everyone says that Supes is a boring boy scout wearing his underwear on the wrong side of his pants. I dare to disagree. Superman is the archetype of a spandex clad super hero. My theory is that he is so good while at the same time being so powerful that it makes people uncomfortable. We have grown too cynical and we well know that we could never be as good as Super</span>
  <span id="freeText5782651683029316728" style="display:none"><a href="https://mateuszcelestyn.wordpress.com/2016/12/03/all-star-superman-vol-1-by-grant-morrison-w-and-frank-quitely-a/" rel="nofollow noopener">You can check out this and my other reviews here :)</a><br><br>I have a theory explaining why good old Superman is so disliked nowadays. Almost everyone says that Supes is a boring boy scout wearing his underwear on the wrong side of his pants. I dare to disagree. Superman is the archetype of a spandex clad super hero. My theory is that he is so good while at the same time being so powerful that it makes people uncomfortable. We have grown too cynical and we well know that we could never be as good as Superman. That is why so many people claim they associate more with a broody spoiled sociopath who beats up poor people at night in order to deal with a childhood trauma. Yeah, a much better role model than a farmer boy who moved to the big city and tries to stay good.<br><br>Until now I have never read any comics about man of steel. When I think about Superman I picture <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZAsDL7f3veM" rel="nofollow noopener">Bruce Timm's and Paul Dini's Justice League </a> and <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sjdnCC6n4xk" rel="nofollow noopener">Max Fleischer's cartoons</a> (current movies have a lot of place for improvement when it comes to Superman's portrayal, although I like Henry Cavill very much). I figured it is about damn time to read what people call the <strong>ultimate</strong> Superman book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349441._SX540_.jpg" alt="superman_all-star_superman_007" width="2048" height="1578" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The tale concocted for us by Grant Morrison boils the man of tomorrow down to his basics. Each issue is a separate story with connected by the foreshadowing of Superman's death. Before he passes away Supes wants to tie all the loose ends ad do as much good as he can. A simplistic story yes, but what is truly important here are not any surprising plot twists but the characters. Superman is portrayed as a <strong>almighty almost divine yet so very tangible</strong> without any of that godawful messiah complex that some like to attach to him. It is mostly achieved because we are allowed an insight into other character's perception of Superman. Why does Lois Lane love him, Jimmy Olsen trusts him, Lex Luthor hates him and what did Jonathan and Martha Kent desire for him? It makes him and his surrounding cast of characters <strong>more human and real than ever</strong>.<br><br>Obviously this book also includes the sillier and more kitsch elements of Superman mythos like the 5th dimension, Supermen Squad, the underverse and the black kryptonite. Quite complicated and silly concepts that would not fit in a darker and more serious book, but here they are introduced and explained in a simple light hearted manner which fits the story and is <strong>not ashamed of them</strong>. Also very important: for the first time in my life I bought into the idea that no-one ever realized Clark Kent and Superman are the same person. Nobody would ever suspect that goofy oaf Kent!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349442._SY540_.jpg" alt="149a638775a8b490fc03a7c1e48cba81" width="1280" height="1977" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The artistic design here is very important. Buildings and clothes look futuristic in a way that people in the 1950's imagined future to be. I think it is perfect for Superman stories. At the same time the design of the characters... Lets face it they are ugly. There is <strong>something very wrong with the faces</strong>, their eyes and overall structure that I can't precisely point out. Yet after the second issue I got used to it and now I actually think that <strong>it compliments the story very well</strong>. Not entirely realistic yet not entirely stylized either. Same thing goes for the colors. Jamie Grant colored it digitally with very bright almost neon gradients. It was very distracting at first but the more of it I saw, the better it suited the story and its atmosphere. <strong>Hopeful bright colors for a hopeful character</strong>. Some panels in here are really touching and simply beautiful. <strong>Especially this one</strong>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349443._SY540_.jpg" alt="superman_all-star_superman_021" width="1024" height="1623" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It shouldn't work yet somehow Morrison and Quitely, <strong>two crazy Scotsmen</strong>, created something truly beautiful. If you want to convince someone into liking Superman, give them this book. If they don't like it, I don't think you need this kind of negativity in your life.<br><p>
  <strong>VERDICT</strong>
</p><br><p>Five out of five friendly piggyback rides.</p><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349444._SX540_.jpg" alt="wpqeyvly" width="509" height="318" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349444._SX540_.jpg" alt="wpqeyvly" width="509" height="318" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349444._SX540_.jpg" alt="wpqeyvly" width="509" height="318" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349444._SX540_.jpg" alt="wpqeyvly" width="509" height="318" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480777660i/21349444._SX540_.jpg" alt="wpqeyvly" width="509" height="318" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tdVtumeCb/tRLJ3zMWBg5vaTkeeAkAFKrGXPEXaszeIv10DqnPMK5lmU/1IKseFAMAeeRk+dfIf/aYaADPp6wg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rao6dUVVu7su7zUNnr68GLpTpTipBLEZ7FpDC1XYGGffqBclviTepiZXV6ylbz2+fMeqmWYJzNS/VgqaL46vRw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer15635243631444958926">Scottish comic book author Grant Morrison is known for culture-jamming and the constant reinvention of their work. They are known for their nonlinear narratives and countercultural leanings in their runs on titles including DC Comics' Animal Man, Batman, JLA, The Invisibles, Action Comics, All-Star Superman, and Doom Patrol, and Marvel Comics' New X-Men and Fantastic Four. Many of these are contro</span>
  <span id="freeText15635243631444958926" style="display:none">Scottish comic book author Grant Morrison is known for culture-jamming and the constant reinvention of their work. They are known for their nonlinear narratives and countercultural leanings in their runs on titles including DC Comics' Animal Man, Batman, JLA, The Invisibles, Action Comics, All-Star Superman, and Doom Patrol, and Marvel Comics' New X-Men and Fantastic Four. Many of these are controversial, yet rate in some of the most critically acclaimed and popular books. They are also active in screenwriting.</span>
